Municipal Government Stipulates the Starting Date for the Issuance of Retirement Pay 102

March 17, 1928

When employers and employees in the city's industrial and commercial sectors terminate their employment relationship, the municipal government has previously stipulated that the retirement pay that should be issued to workers in accordance with the Measures for Retirement Benefits for Employees should be calculated from the date of implementation of the measures. However, there are two Provisional Measures for Retirement Benefits for Employees in this city. One was formulated by the former Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce based on the provisions of Articles 31 and 34 of the revised Provisional Regulations for Labor-Capital Mediation in Shanghai Special Municipality. The full text consists of nine articles and was submitted to the municipal government for approval and promulgation on March 17, 1928. Later, after the central government promulgated the Law on the Handling of Labor-Capital Disputes, this city revised the Provisional Regulations for Labor-Capital Mediation, explicitly abolishing the previous regulations. The previous measures thus became invalid. The other was that the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs believed that the previous measures had become invalid, so it formulated new measures with reference to them. The full text consists of fifteen articles and was promulgated by the municipal government on November 3, 1928. Although the provisions of the two measures on the issuance of retirement pay to workers are generally the same, the dates of promulgation and implementation are eight months apart. There are no explicit provisions on the date from which the issuance of retirement pay to workers should be calculated. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs believed that the matter was related to the interests of workers and specially requested the municipal government to review and instruct on how to handle it. The municipal government believed that when employers and employees established an employment relationship after the promulgation of the measures before March 17, 1928, they had the obligation to bear the issuance of retirement pay. All retirement pay issued to workers can be pushed back to the date of promulgation of the measures before March 17, 1928, to show consideration for the difficulties of workers. It has already instructed the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to comply and handle it yesterday.

Xu Clan Descendants Urgently Request Preservation of the Grand Secretary Memorial Archway 115

Document Presented to the Municipal Government

The Grand Secretary Memorial Archway on Zhaojia Road (inside the Great South Gate) in this city was built by the descendants of Xu Guangqi, the Grand Secretary of the Ming Dynasty, who was posthumously awarded the title of Grand Protector, using funds raised by them. It is the only historical site of a famous official in Shanghai for 300 years. Recently, it was learned that the Bureau of Public Works has a proposal to demolish the Grand Secretary Memorial Archway. Upon hearing this, the Xu clan was shocked. Yesterday, more than 20 people from the clan, including Xu Chengzong, Xu Ren, Xu Muguo, and Xu Jiyun, jointly presented a petition to the Municipal Government, requesting the preservation of the historical site. The original text is copied below:

Presentation regarding the Grand Secretary Memorial Archway, which concerns the historical site of a famous official, urgently requesting instructions to the Bureau of Public Works to preserve it in order to respect predecessors and follow public opinion.

On May 10th of this year, a notice was received from the Land Bureau stating, "It is approved that the Bureau of Public Works has sent a letter inquiring whether the stone archway at the intersection of County Foundation Road and Zhaojia Road is public or private property, or whether it is a historical site, and requesting that it be investigated and reported." Accordingly, the Xu family was notified to collect and submit the single chain deeds to the bureau for inspection in order to verify the information. The citizen Jiyun immediately submitted the single chain and stated that this archway is a private building related to the historical site of the local sage and should be preserved, and submitted a document to the Land Bureau for reply. Recently, it has been learned that the Bureau of Public Works has a proposal to submit to the government for approval to demolish the Grand Secretary Memorial Archway due to road administration. It is not certain whether the news is true, but the citizens are all descendants of the Grand Secretary Wending Gong, and upon hearing this, they are shocked and cannot sleep peacefully.

It is maintained that the Grand Secretary of the Ming Dynasty, who was posthumously awarded the title of Grand Protector, enshrined in the county and township temples, and the ninth ancestor of the citizens, whose name was Guangqi and posthumous title was Wending Gong, was specially ordered to build this archway after his death in the sixth year of Chongzhen. Construction began in the Ming Dynasty, but was interrupted due to the change of dynasties. It was not until the early years of the Kangxi reign of the Qing Dynasty that the archway was completed by the descendants of the Xu clan, using funds raised by them. It is recorded in the provincial, prefectural, and county records. For 300 years, it has been protected by local officials, because the Grand Secretary Wending's merits, career, scholarship, and economy shook the past and the present. His lifelong works, such as the Complete Treatise on Agricultural Administration, and dozens of other books, are all related to national economy and people's livelihood and benefit future generations. He is truly a famous official and a great Confucian of the Ming Dynasty, who is admired both at home and abroad. Erecting a stone archway is to admire his former achievements and commemorate the local sage. It is not only related to the historical sites of the previous dynasty and local anecdotes. As for the foundation of the archway, it was purchased by the Xu clan, and from the early Qing Dynasty to the present, it has been managed by the descendants of the Xu clan and the taxes have been paid in full. It is indeed private property and not within the scope of public land. The citizens invited the clan to gather and discuss, and all agreed that stone archways are erected outside the city, and none of them have been demolished. Why is it that the ancient historical site of our ancestors, a private building, is not preserved? Public sentiment is surging, and all are advocating preservation. For this reason, they urgently petition jointly. In addition to presenting to the Bureau of Public Works, they humbly request that Your Excellency quickly instruct the Bureau of Public Works to grant approval and consider that this Grand Secretary Memorial Archway is the only historical site of a famous official in Shanghai for 300 years, follow the order of the Ministry of Interior to allow preservation, withdraw the order to demolish the archway, so as to respect the local sage and last forever. Both the living and the dead will be grateful.

Six-Year-Old Girl Pregnant 116

Eats a Bun and Has a Monstrous Fetus

Will Come to Shanghai Soon for Public Display

Zhuo Xiang'geng, director of the Wusong Ship Donation Sub-Office of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, is from Fenghua, eastern Zhejiang. Yesterday, he received a letter from his hometown stating that in the countryside of Fenghua, a farmer named Wu Daogen married a woman named Xu, who gave birth to a girl in 1925. The girl is now six years old. After the girl was born, there were no unusual signs, just like a normal child. Unexpectedly, around December of last year, she accidentally ate a rice bun, and from then on, the order of her development suddenly changed. Her hair and teeth grew, and her abdomen gradually swelled. Recently, her abdomen has become as big as a drum. Wu initially thought that his daughter was sick due to indigestion and consulted a doctor, but according to the doctor's examination, the girl had no illness at all. After much research, it was determined that the swollen abdomen actually contained a monstrous fetus. After this news spread, it caused a sensation in the surrounding areas, and it was regarded as a strange event. It is said that Mr. Huang, a Shanghai businessman, heard about it and has sent someone by boat to Ningbo and then to Fenghua to negotiate terms with Wu and hire him at a high price. Wu will soon lead the girl to Shanghai for display in a room at the Great World for tourists to observe and study.

Injured Female Corpse Found on Wasteland on Xietu Road 117

Four Knife Wounds on the Face

Two Knife Wounds on the Hands

Yesterday morning, a dog manure collector discovered a murdered female corpse on the wasteland south of the Yan Family Cemetery on Xietu Road in Shanghai. Shocked, he shouted for help. The police from the 2nd District Police Station were dispatched to investigate and found that the female corpse was about thirty years old, wearing a black serge jacket and blue calico trousers. Prosecutor Lei was commissioned to go to the scene for inspection. Direct Shanghai-Tianjin Telegraph Line Re-established 118

Restoration to Original State

Since Yan and Feng initiated the rebellion, the direct Tianjin line of the China Telegraph Administration had been blocked. North China telecommunications relied only on the Ershui line to Yantai and the direct land line to Qingdao for relay. Recently, since the Northeast supported the Central Government and Yan's rebellion collapsed, the direct Shanghai-Tianjin line was reported to be open at noon the day before yesterday. From then on, telecommunications traffic in North China has returned to the agile and good original state of unification last year. From yesterday, the Sichuan Road China Telegraph Administration, the Telegraph North Bureau behind the Jianchu Savings Association on Fusheng Road in Zhabei, and the Xiaodongmen Telegraph South Bureau accepted all telegrams sent from Shanghai to the North Road, which were unusually crowded.

Municipal Government Orders Bureaus to Ban the Use of Gloss Powder in Rice Milling 122

The Municipal Government issued an order to the Social Affairs and Public Security Bureaus yesterday, stating that in order to implement the matter, it was previously reported by the bureaus that the gloss powder used in rice milling was found to be non-toxic and that it was proposed to limit the amount used. The matter was then reported to the Executive Yuan for review and instructed to be informed. Now, Order No. 2771 of the Executive Yuan states, "The report has been received. It has been found that adding mineral white powder, namely carbonic acid, to rice milling in excessive amounts is harmful to digestion. Please still instruct the ban to be enforced to ensure people's food." This order, etc. Therefore, in addition to issuing separate orders, it is hereby ordered that the bureaus comply with the order.

Demolish and Sell the Zunjing Pavilion of the Confucius Temple 123

Remove Stone Tablets for Preservation

The Confucius Temple Zunjing Pavilion on Confucius Temple Road in this city is built behind the Minglun Hall and was formerly a place for storing books. It is one of the historical sites in Shanghai. However, the pavilion has been in disrepair for a long time and is about to collapse. Members of the Municipal Education and Public Works Bureaus have been sent to investigate and all agreed that if it is to be preserved, it must be repaired quickly. As for the repair cost, it is estimated to be about 10,000 yuan. In a time when the municipal treasury is empty, it is factually difficult to do so. After consultation between the two bureaus, it was decided that although the pavilion is a historical site and should be preserved, the damage is so severe and the danger is so great that if it is not repaired, it should be demolished and sold. Currently, the Bureau of Public Works has hired workers to remove the stone tablets on the wall of the pavilion and place them elsewhere for remembrance, and has issued a notice inviting bids for demolition and sale.

Wang Guofang's Words Anger Anhui People 124

Anhui People's Lives Only Require 3,000 Yuan to Prepare

The Entire Factory's Workers Mobilize Public Outrage

Dong Dexing Files a Lawsuit

Dong Dexing, 24 years old, from Hefei, lives at 796 Jichengfang, Taopeng Road. He currently works in the velvet carpet section of the Jardine Matheson Cotton Mill. He recently accused the mill's foremen Wang Guofang, Wang Jiekui, and Wang Jiexian, as well as Jiekui's brother-in-law Wu Qingbao, Wang Qingxiang, Zhang Ruijia, and others, of attempted murder. The facts he alleged are roughly as follows: The plaintiff worked at Jardine Matheson, and his wages were calculated based on the amount of work done. On the fourth day of last month, Wang Jiekui suddenly stopped issuing manufacturing materials, making it impossible to work. Later, when he asked Jiekui's brother-in-law for materials, he was refused and beaten instead. Wang Guofang also helped with the assault, declaring that killing an Anhui person only required preparing 3,000 yuan to settle the matter. This provoked the public outrage of all the Anhui workers in the factory, who went on strike. On the morning of the eighth of that month, the plaintiff and Wang Xirong went to Jiekui's house, where Wang Qingbao, Wang Qingxiang, Zhang Ruijia, and others, under his command, used axes to violently chop the plaintiff after he fell. They continued to chop him as many as thirteen times, causing serious injuries to his hands, feet, lower abdomen, and other parts. Later, he was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment by his fellow villager Zhang Songbai. After more than 40 days, he has not yet recovered. He requested that the defendants be summoned to court for interrogation and attached a private lawsuit seeking compensation of 10,000 yuan. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Cheng Shangfeng of the Special District Court summoned the defendants for interrogation. The defendants hired lawyers Chen Tingrui, Fan Gang, and Ni Gang for defense, while only Jiekui, Jiexian, and Guofang surrendered themselves. Their testimonies were mostly evasive and disclaimed responsibility. The plaintiff Dong Dexing arrived in court with his wounds and described the process of being assaulted by Wang and others. Ye Xirong testified. After reviewing the case, Judge Cheng ordered the defendant Wang Jiekui to be detained, Wang Jiexian and Wang Guofang to each pay a bail of 1,000 yuan, and postponed the hearing for seven days to summon the remaining defendants for further interrogation.

Such is the fate of speculators.

Zhu Shiseng's Letter to the Gengxin Theater 144

Zhu Shiseng's letter to the Gengxin Theater states: Greetings. The scenery, singing, and acting of the "Journey to the West" performed by your theater are all exquisite. I am deeply impressed by your hard work and dedication. It is not only captivating and can make your business flourish, but it can also transform people's hearts and create a bright path in society. I believe that the merits of the initiators, those in charge, and all those who embody the teachings are immeasurable. The goodness of society depends entirely on the commercial activities that spread throughout. Most ordinary businesses are for self-interest and rarely consider public morality. Now, your theater takes public morality as its guide and can seek benefits for the public, while its own interests are also contained within. In other words, if society is mired in hardship, how can one be exempt? If society is at peace and people live in contentment, then one should share it. Therefore, to be at peace, one must first seek the peace of the masses. Your theater is full every day. Is this not a call to transform? Is this not clear evidence that fame and fortune can be shared? I have a request. Although the actors are not living Buddhas, Bodhisattvas, true immortals, or true deities, their actions are representative. Therefore, I ask that you pay special attention to your words and actions. One word can bring immeasurable blessings, and one word can sow many seeds of disaster. Please give more lectures on the words of benefit. You will surely have a great future, and all things will be as you wish. Buddhas greet people by putting their palms together, not by raising one hand. When anyone sees a Buddha or Bodhisattva, they should put their palms together and say "Namo Amitabha Buddha" and bow once or three times (Buddhist rules require three bows to make a complete prostration). Bodhisattvas hold a pure water bottle in one hand and a willow branch in the other. They use the pure water from the bottle and the willow branch to sprinkle, washing away the karma of the masses and purifying them. Please decorate the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas in a moving and pleasing manner and make improvements. I hope that you will embody the teachings and restore the morals of society and guide them to the path of goodness. It is easy to persuade people on the stage. The audience's spirits are completely focused. Earnestly guide them, and I have high hopes for you all. I have enclosed 20 copies each of my "Wide and Long Tongue" volumes 1, 2, and 3 for your reference. If there is anything of value, please do not discard them casually.

Xu Gongshu's Reply to Accountant Pan Zhaobang 147

Xu Gongshu's letter to accountant Pan Zhaobang yesterday stated: I received your letter of September 26th regarding the collection of shares for the Moral Bank, which has been advertised in newspapers. The Moral Bank, originally named the World Moral Society Savings Bank, was initiated by the World Moral Society and was intended solely for the savings of members. It had no external business and no non-member shareholders. Zheng Deqi and I were in the process of preparing to establish the bank and drafting the establishment contract when we received Order No. 1674 from the Social Bureau, which stated that societies are not allowed to establish banks and ordered us to stop. Later, we received Approval No. 472 from the Municipal Government, stating that we were not allowed to proceed with preparations for opening a bank until it had been approved. Therefore, we dared not proceed and immediately ended the process in accordance with the order. On February 1, 1930, we severed ties with the bank, which had not been approved by the government. Zheng Deqi alone was responsible for all affairs of the bank and whether to continue its opening. Zheng Deqi separately recruited shareholders and reorganized the bank into the Moral Commercial Bank to avoid investigation. At the same time, we reported the termination in accordance with the order to the Social Bureau for approval. We were concerned about not being able to recover the money that had already been paid, and naturally there was no reason to pay any further shares. Due to the above reasons, I am responding to your letter accordingly. Please investigate and inform Zheng Deqi (omitted below).

News from Various Labor Unions 149

The Postal Workers Union held its second executive committee meeting the day before yesterday. Chairman Zhu Xuefan performed the ceremony as usual and reported on the following matters: (Omitted.) Matters for discussion: (1) The regulations for various examinations in Postal Administration Order No. 629 are inadequate. Colleagues from various regions have requested the General Administration to revise them. The union has also sent people to review how to handle the matter. Resolution: (A) Request to abolish the performance and advanced examination. (B) Conduct primary and advanced postal worker examinations once a year, as well as promotion examinations. All postal workers at the fourth grade, first level, and above may participate. Each person may take each examination up to three times. Those who pass each examination will be promoted three levels. Those who do not wish to take the examination or fail will be promoted based on seniority to the highest salary level without restriction. (C) When no outsiders participate in the examination, an additional 30 points will be added to the total score for Jiang Patrol Police and Mail Carriers who participate in the Postal Assistant examination. An additional 40 points will be added to the total score for Postal Assistants in the Postal Worker Qualifying Examination. (B) Send a circular to friendly unions in various regions to unanimously advocate for this. (2) How to handle the case where all extra workers submit three resolutions passed at the general meeting on September 29th and request approval for implementation. Resolution: (A) Request the authorities to hold the Postal Assistant examination at least once a year. (B) Those who have not been promoted to Postal Assistant after three years will be transferred to the worker class. Passed. (C) Revision of the promotion salary, rejected. (3) Case where the authorities continue to assign hard laborers to work even after their work hours have been completed. Resolution: For each hour of continued work, a subsidy of 15 cents should be given. However, the authorities may not force assignment if the person does not agree. (4) Proposal from the Construction Department that Qiu Jingmei and over 30 other members request the union to establish an art division, with an attached list of estimated start-up costs. Is it feasible? Resolution: Retained. (5) Omitted. (6) Based on the first standing committee resolution of the Supervisory Committee, the first case requests the designation of responsible personnel to jointly examine the economic situation of the 7th session with the supervisory committee members and prepare a detailed report for public announcement to all members. Resolution: Designate Executive Committee members Zhuang Zhengxin and the Economic Minister on duty, and three other members to jointly review and report to the Supervisory Committee in detail for public announcement. A Little Laugh 151

— Hai Ke

Man—Darling. I implore you with 120% sincerity. Be mine, won't you?

Woman—No. I'm determined not to marry. Determined not to be bound by any man.

Man—Then, would it be okay if I were yours?

An absent-minded university professor (waking up in the morning and seeing a large flower ball on his desk)—Hmm. What is this? Who sent this flower ball?

His wife—My love. This is from me to you. Don't you remember? Today is our wedding anniversary.

Absent-minded university professor—Ah. I see. Then what day is your wedding anniversary? I'll also send you a flower ball.

Woman—Darling. Have you spoken to Father yet?

Man—Yes, I have.

Woman—What did the old man say?

Man—He was initially cold. When I spoke to him, he ignored me.

Woman—Did you explain your intention to propose marriage and mention that you have five thousand yuan in the bank?

Man—I only mentioned the deposit. Before I could get to the proposal, he said, "(Very good. Lend it to me, then.)"

A Record of Two Great Unjust Cases in Rongcheng 152

— Qing Song Jushi

Near the Da Wu Bridge inside the Tongbo Gate of Songyi, there was a man named Hu Yinglong, from a scholarly family. His parents died early. He worked in a bank, living frugally and managing to make ends meet. The year before last, he married a woman named Zhang. The Zhang family was originally prominent. Zhang was by nature silent and did not smile easily, possessing the demeanor of a noble lady. Her uncle, named Xinpu, died early without an heir, leaving only a widow, the well-known Nie. Although Yinglong was the only son of his branch, he was responsible for continuing the lineage and should take her as his step-mother. In name, the aunt was like a mother. The aunt was beautiful and cunning, and although she was a widow whose age was past her prime, she was still skilled at dressing herself up. Looking at her, she appeared to be a beautiful woman in her early twenties. She usually relied on her beauty and was lively, still possessing a spring-like charm that kept people awake at night. Her inquiries and care for her nephew were no different from a loving mother's protection of her infant. However, she treated her nephew's wife with arrogance and condescension, much like imperialists looking down from above. Although there were many complaints from outsiders, Zhang always followed the rules and respected her mother-in-law, never speaking harshly or showing anger. Even when she returned to her mother's home, she never revealed any complaints when discussing family matters with her mother (Zhang's father was deceased, but her mother was still alive), siblings, and sisters about her husband's family, so how could her seclusion, virtuousness, and quietness be described?

This year, she had returned to her mother's home twice. Afterward, she returned due to business. It had only been a little over ten days when, on the 31st day, bad news arrived. Before the incident, no signs of illness had been heard, and after the incident, the truth was unknown. There were no doubts about the suspicious points. Zhang's mother, younger brother, and sisters rushed to her home, weeping loudly over the corpse. Even if it was for the sake of settling the matter and pacifying the people, they did not want to stir up a big wave. However, rumors were rife, and the deceased had died unjustly. How could they vent their anger and appeal for justice? Therefore, they appealed to the court. On one hand, they summoned her husband and aunt for interrogation and detention. On the other hand, they asked a doctor to examine the body and fill out the injury report. Since then, although there have been no repeated and strict interrogations, it is not known who issued the release instructions. However, it is not difficult to imagine from the clues.

A few days later, outside the Guyang Gate on the west street of Cang Bridge, there was another assassination of Tang Zhibei. Tang started his business from nothing and had talent. He set up a paint shop in the west market of Cang Bridge, using extraordinary methods to make profits, studying Yi Dun's methods, and holding calculations and techniques. Therefore, he accumulated a considerable amount of wealth, and there were many who coveted it. His son, named Qiusheng, was addicted to smoking, gambling, and debauchery. He often associated with the lowest classes, using money like dirt. Although Tang rebuked him with kindness, not only was it difficult to change his nature, but he became even more willful and tyrannical. Therefore, it became more unbearable, and the father and son quarreled.

Tang also had a residence in addition to the shop. Looking across the street, the scale was magnificent. He habitually left in the morning and returned in the evening. Recently, he had been busy with shop matters and lacked people to take care of him, so he stayed at the back of the shop to avoid the trouble of going back and forth. Unexpectedly, at midnight three days ago, he was suddenly attacked by thugs who stabbed him several times in the chest and abdomen. The flesh and blood were blurred, and the manner of death was extremely tragic. Whether it was revenge or banditry was unknown. However, Tang's lodging place was quite deep and secluded. Those who were not familiar with the entrance would certainly not be able to enter. Where did the thugs come from? After they entered the hall and room, they did not steal goods but killed people. There is no such reason in the world. Although the perpetrator disappeared without a trace, only the suspect was summoned for interrogation. The truth is not yet clear, and public opinion outside has pointed out many things. It is thought that clues can be found.

After the Abolition of the Death Penalty 153

— Ying Dai

Recently, countries around the world, for the sake of humanitarianism, have made proposals to abolish the death penalty. However, whether the abolition of the death penalty can make criminals realize their mistakes and reduce homicides is a major problem. Among them, such as Austria in Europe, the death penalty was once abolished. However, after the abolition of the death penalty, the number of murderers suddenly increased. For example, if we compare the recent records of murderers with those from ten years ago, the difference is several times greater. After the abolition of the death penalty, criminals, even if they commit the most serious crimes, will not be put to death, so they have no more scruples. From this perspective, the abolition of the death penalty not only fails to reduce criminals but also increases serious crimes. Therefore, France has strongly opposed this proposal. The implementation of the abolition of the death penalty may not become a reality for the time being.

Advice to Young Women: Don't Marry an Athlete 154

— Ye Xin Fo

A wonderful hand on the ball field, a track and field hero, all those with beautiful qualities favor them. Now, the wife of a certain British athlete has published a wonderful article, advising young women, given her husband's lack of affection, not to marry a man of athletics. I now translate it as follows for the amusement of readers.

All you young women, before marrying an athlete, there is much to consider. The life and interests of an athlete are completely devoted to sports, and they have little emotional understanding. Therefore, the lack of knowledge among today's athletes has become a common phenomenon. Even at the age of forty, they are still as ignorant and charming as elementary school students. Readers, do not think that such a young student is enough to please people. Little do we women know that the husband of our dreams must be emotionally considerate and spiritually focused, as the most important conditions. Otherwise, they will be constantly competing in the arena, and the feelings between husband and wife will be damaged. The loneliness of the heart is even greater than the physical one.

Furthermore, athletes have no peace and quiet for a moment, as if they have lost something. Their only glory is not in love, but in sports. Their only entertainment is not in heart-to-heart talks, but in competition. As for literary recreation and appreciation, it is not worth mentioning. Their readings are limited to childish novels and biographies of famous athletes. When they read newspapers, they first grab the sports news and read it. If you touch their anger, they will laugh foolishly. International news and social trivia have nothing to do with them. If their team is defeated, it will keep them awake all night. They usually sleep soundly, snoring like cattle, even if the country is in danger, it is not enough to disturb their sweet dreams. In social gatherings, people are happy to talk, but they sit woodenly in a corner. If Hobbs or Bradman (these two are famous athletes) are mentioned, their excitement will be uncontrollable. For a moment, everyone's eyes will be on them. The above is not enough to describe them even in one ten-thousandth. In my humble opinion (as the author calls herself), an athletic man should be matched with an athletic woman, so that they can share the same interests and compete in the art of skills every day, taking the ball field as their home and sports as their life. As they get older, they may have the opportunity to read together under the lamp. Is this true or not? It is still up to the wives of athletes to judge.

A Secretary-General Whose Moves are Impossible to Predict 155

— Feng

Unadorned and virtuous officials like those of the two Han dynasties are not easily found in modern times. When there is an elder with both virtue and goodness, people always praise them, which is also a slightly fair intention. Since Zhejiang Province has been under the revolutionary government, the administration has been clear and honest, leading the country. The officials in various departments of the provincial capital are all self-disciplined, honest, and self-respecting. This has been the case for many terms, and it has almost become a custom. Among them, the Secretariat of the Provincial Government is the most prominent. Successive secretaries-general, such as Chen Qihuai and Shen Shiyuan, were known for their morality and writing skills. They were all rare talents who were both excellent in Confucian studies and diligent in official affairs. The most recent successor to this position is Mr. Liu Shixin, former member of the Purge Committee of Guangzhou Special Municipality. He is young and vigorous, with extraordinary courage and insight. He is diligent in public affairs day and night, and Chairman Zhang Jingjiang appreciates him very much. Liu is from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province. He graduated from the University of Lyon in France. He has served as the principal, teacher, and newspaper editor of Chinese schools in the British and Dutch colonies of Nanyang. After returning to China, he served as a full-time lecturer at Guangdong University and Sun Yat-sen University, as well as the secretary and section chief of the Guangdong Provincial Department of Agriculture and Industry Construction, and a member of the Guangzhou Municipal Party Committee Reorganization Committee. He worked hard during the purge, and important figures in the party praised him greatly. In the seventeenth year, when Zhang Jingjiang took over the Zhejiang government, Liu was appointed secretary until now. He is shrewd, experienced, humble, and amiable. Since his promotion to Secretary-General, he has become even more diligent and self-motivated, setting an example for the department. His attitude towards his colleagues is sincere and cordial. Every day, he personally goes to the general office to discuss various matters, tirelessly teaching people. Therefore, his colleagues all respect and love him. However, Liu likes to wear Chinese clothing and cloth-soled shoes, and his steps are light and silent. Officials sometimes do not notice, and Liu has already arrived. Therefore, everyone secretly says that the Secretary-General comes and goes so suddenly, which is really a suffering that is impossible to guard against. It is also a great conversation starter in political circles.

The Finnish Farmers' Anti-Communist Movement (4) 157

— Liu Zeng, sent from Paris

After the government submitted the anti-communist bill to parliament, it was opened that due to the weakness of the communist presence in parliament, it feared that a majority of members would not agree. Therefore, before the bill was voted on, the entire cabinet resigned. P. E. Svinhfuvud, a Finnish independence fighter who had been exiled to Siberia by the Russians, organized a purely bourgeois party cabinet. Therefore, the government's anti-communist attitude was even stricter than before. According to Svinhufvud's declaration, the government's plan to eliminate communism was to disregard everything and not stop until the goal was achieved.

No matter how orderly a country is, when a large mass movement passes, it is often accompanied by a few violent scenes. Therefore, while the government was dealing with the Communist Party in parliament with legitimate means, the Lapua movement acted freely. The situation of their riots has been reported in various newspapers and will not be repeated here. After the incident, the government worked hard to suppress it and obtained the understanding of the leaders of the Lapua movement. The riots immediately stopped.

After the dissolution of parliament, the new Minister of Interior found that the communist members of parliament were suspected of violating the law and ordered their arrest. At the same time, the Communist Party's disguised workers and small peasant party were declared illegal because they had accepted and implemented orders from Moscow.

Now the new parliamentary election is approaching. It is heard that the new cabinet has adopted the Lapua movement's proposal and formulated various plans to change the existing election law to ensure that the Communist Party will disappear from the Finnish parliament in the future.

In short, from a historical perspective, the so-called Lapua movement, although known to the world for its recent riots, has been brewing for almost as long as the Communist Party's activities in Finland. At first, it was just an expression of the simple patriotism of the farmers. Later, after the instigation of religious figures and the agitation of politicians, it wanted to become a political movement. Although the leaders of the Lapua movement now claim that the Lapua movement has no other political ambitions, the current cabinet wants to rely on its power to deal with the Communist Party. The power of the Lapua movement will become more and more prosperous and will undoubtedly become a major organization dominating the Finnish political situation.

Warmth in My Heart (286) 158

— Bao Xiao Tian

Chapter 14: Green Bamboo Tears, Her Heart Breaks; Red Lotus Fragrance Fades, a Girl's Soul Departs

At this time, Zhang Yiqing was out fooling around again. As the saying goes, "Having obtained what is needed, he seeks more." He felt bored at home and stayed out late again. His wife was not as strict with him as before. Previously, Zhang Yiqing claimed that he was going to Hankou by boat, but he was actually hiding in a small house. Now, he really went to Hankou by boat. It wasn't that the comprador of the steamship was suddenly diligent; it was because he could avoid the ears and eyes of Shanghai and do whatever he wanted in Hankou. Sometimes, he wouldn't return for several ships. Some people even said that he had a mistress in Hankou. On this side, the woman in Shanghai unleashed her jealous fury. Because Zhang Yiqing was not at home, she would take it out on Cuiyun at every turn. At first, it was just cold words, and Cuiyun ignored her. Later, she simply started cursing. When the Ningbo old woman's temper flared up, she would scold anything. At first, Cuiyun retorted, but in the end, she couldn't win against her. All struggles for gain and advantage rely on wealth and power as backup. That Ningbo old woman, relying on her wealth and power, had her whole family helping her. Zhang Yiqing was not even in their eyes, let alone Cuiyun. In their eyes, she was a concubine bought with money. Although the master bought her with money, the master's money was given by the madam. So it could be said that she was bought by the madam. When you're bought, you have to do whatever they say. Is there any room for resistance? At that time, Cuiyun felt as if she were in a tiger's den, unable to clap with one hand. When Zhang Yiqing was at home, she could still complain to him. Zhang Yiqing would still comfort her a little. But later, Zhang Yiqing had taken another fancy to someone else and was no longer interested in Cuiyun. Hearing her talk on and on, saying things that made people uncomfortable, he also felt annoyed. Moreover, even if she told Zhang Yiqing, it wouldn't mean that the east wind would prevail over the west wind. She would even be influenced by the woman's words and blame Cuiyun instead, saying that she should give in because of her position. Later, that woman would also complain to Zhang Yiqing about Cuiyun, pointing out all sorts of faults. After all, she came from a brothel and was not fit to be a family member, without any poise. Of course, she would say a word, finding fault with others, and adding fuel to the fire, adding many ingredients to make it sound appealing. Zhang Yiqing gradually began to say that Cuiyun was wrong. Every day, he would prepare opium for her until almost dawn. He would sleep until sunset, while Cuiyun, if she got up late, would be called lazy. She was still in the habit of a brothel girl. They said that because she got up late, the female servants in the house were learning from her and also getting up late. That Ningbo old woman used all sorts of tricks to trick Cuiyun into canceling the small house and moving in with her. It was a kind of tactic to slowly abuse her, making it impossible for her to stay. So it was no good no matter which way she turned. Picking bones out of an egg, carving patterns on ivory chopsticks, putting her in a dead end.

The Decline in the Financial and Gold Market 159

Often Accompanied by Minor Storms. The gold market situation for the past two days has turned downward again. However, there are often hidden surges, drifting aimlessly. There were about three or four taels of rotation, totaling seven taels of fluctuating silver throughout the day. However, it has broken through the 70-tael mark. This is because the foreign exchange trend is declining, and although there is buying in the gold industry, most banks have supplies, which has caused the market to loosen. Major firms, speculators, and others have been quick to sell. Yuan Mao Yong, Yuan Xing Yong, Yong Yong Heng, and others have sold, while Jin An Wan Xing Shunli and others have bought since the early market opened at a low level. This is likely because the silver market is not moving, and there are still many sellers. However, subsequent recoveries and repetitions were intertwined, hovering around 70 taels. Later, Yuan Mao Yong, Bing Xing, and others first sold, but Zhifeng Yong, Jin An, and others were buying positions. Initially, it was weak, but then, with the increase in Indian exchange telegraphic transfers, it once fell to between 66 taels. However, because Zhifeng Yong and others were eager to buy, it immediately rose, reaching the 70-tael mark. However, the exchange rate became increasingly loose, and Yong Heng and others inclined to sell, still falling by two or three taels. The final price was about 68 taels. Overall, people's minds are divided.

Early Opening Sees Low盘. The gold standard for November opened low in the morning, decreasing by one tael and eight maces, to 70 taels and four maces (but the gross rate reached 68 taels). Although there were no major gains or losses, people were restless. Shortly after, Yifeng, Yong, and others bought, immediately jumping up by more than one tael to 73 taels and eight maces. However, buyers rose up, and Yuan Cheng Yong and others, as well as hedgers, sold, resulting in a sharp drop of more than six taels, to only 67 taels and a half. Shunli and Han Heng and others subsequently bought. Foreign banks mutually traded January British gold at 7 pence 375, so the published price rose to 70 taels. No change was made to the listed price. McCarly bought December British gold at 7 pence 25, and Union Transport Holland mutually traded December U.S. gold at 39 yuan 125, so it rose to 71 taels 67 maces. Subsequently, due to the British gold for this month being traded at 7 pence 25, and Sumitomo issuing U.S. gold at 39 yuan 1875, it fell back by more than two taels. At 10 o'clock, it was 69 taels and three maces. Suddenly, Xinfeng and others entered the market and took positions, and the market situation turned firm, rising sharply by four taels. Around 10:30, it was 73 taels 12 maces. Later, Yong Heng and others sold, and Xianling and others saw firmness. Banks had a strong intention to sell. After 10:45, it had fallen to within 69 taels. At 11 o'clock, because Shunli and others bought, and China banks absorbed forward British gold at 7 pence 375, it rose to 72 taels. However, all exchange rates were still loose, and this month could be settled at 7 pence 25, making it difficult to stand firm. It rose again by four taels, to 68 taels 23 maces. At noon closing, it was 68 taels and nine maces. The published price was still 624 taels and six maces, with a discount of 53 to 54 taels, then 51 taels, and 56 taels at noon.

Declined Four Tael, Two Maces. The market opened at 68 taels and one mace, then Yuan Mao Yong and others sold. It rose slightly and then, with the large increase in the Indian exchange rate and the sale by Yuancheng and others, it fell by more than two taels. At 2:30, it was only 66 taels and one mace. British gold in this month traded with French gold at 125. Then, in November, HSBC and others sold 375. After 2 o'clock, Zhifeng Yong and hedgers came to buy, and for a time the momentum was upward, gradually rising by four taels. However, there was a one-tael surge. At 3:45, it reached 70 taels and one mace. However, the exchange rate was still loose, so the price fell again. Yong Heng, Hong Li, Fuyu, and others sold, and it suddenly fell by three taels. After 4 o'clock, it was 67 taels. There was a one-tael fluctuation during the transfer. British gold for this month could be settled at 7 pence 3125. At the 4:30 closing, it was 68 taels and rebounded. Compared to before the holiday (September 30), it fell by four taels and two maces. The largest price during the day was 73 taels and eight maces, and the smallest price was 66 taels and one mace, with a fluctuation of seven taels and seven maces. The published price was discounted by a small amount of 56 to 57 taels. Account balance for October 73 taels in the morning, November 69 taels, replenishment 73 taels, and 72 taels in the afternoon. Now that the days are getting shorter, the account balance after lunch has been changed to 4 o'clock, based on the market price at that time. Goods opened in the morning at 70 taels and four maces, closed at noon at 69 taels, 8 taels and two maces in the afternoon, and 8 taels and four maces at closing.

Few Entered, Many Sold. Most firms mostly sold. Yuan Mao Yong, Yong Heng, Heng Xing, Yuan Cheng Yong, Shun, Chunfa Yong, Fuyu, Yuan Da Yong, and others sold. Yu Da, Da De Cheng, Wan, Yi Feng Yong, and others sold and bought in uneven amounts. Cheng Feng Yong, Shunli, Yongkang, Xin Heng, De Heng, Jin An, and Taikang Run all bought. Zhifeng Yong bought and sold. In the afternoon, Zhifeng Yong, Heng Xing, Jin An, Shunli, Wan Xing, and Yuan Cheng Yong all bought. Bing Xing, Yuan Cheng Yuan Mao Yong, Hong Li, Fuyu, Yong Heng, and Chun Yuan Yong all sold. There were also various firms whose purchases and sales were not fixed. The Dalian gang had a strong buying spirit, buying 3,600 to 3,700 bars and selling 1,000 bars. The Guangdong gang sold approximately 1,000 bars.

Decline in Domestic Foreign Exchange 160

Recently, the price of 条银 has shown a tendency to rise again

Yesterday, there were no changes in the overseas silver market. However, the British and American exchange rates were low, and the Yokohama and Kobe exchange rates rose slightly. HSBC's listed exchange rates did not rise or fall, but the domestic prices generally trended downwards. The near-term rates were especially loose, and appeared to be pulling away from forward rates. The gold market was also weakening, breaking through the 70-tael level, as major firms sold. As a result, compared to the day before yesterday, British gold rose by 1875, American gold rose by 375, and Japanese gold fell by 75. Chinese speculators and the Dalian gang mostly bought, but banks were willing to sell, so the market atmosphere trended downward. The volume of British gold traded was 300,000 pounds, with interbank transactions of 100,000 pounds. The gold industry sold tens of thousands of pounds. McCarly and the East Asia Bank took positions, and Heng Xing and Fuchang settled over 100,000 pounds, sold by HSBC, McCarly, and others. There were more settlements in the afternoon, with some gold hedging. American gold settled at 200,000 yuan, sold by Sumitomo and Mitsui, with interbank transactions of 100,000 yuan. Japanese gold was settled at tens of thousands of yuan by the Dalian gang. Mitsui and Taiwan also sold 100,000 yuan to Mitsubishi. However, people were confused, and the market atmosphere was volatile and uncertain. It is predicted that 条银 may rebound.

The domestic British exchange market fluctuated by 1875 throughout the day, with active trading. The morning prices for October were 1 shilling 7 pence 125, November 1875, December 25, January 3125, with buying prices according to 0625. The noon closing prices for October were 25, November was similar due to the roll-over for hedging, December 3125, and January 375. The afternoon closing prices for October and November were both 3125, December 375, and January 4375, with buying prices according to the record of 0625.

The domestic American exchange market fluctuated by 3125. The morning prices for October were 38 yuan 75, November 875, December 39 yuan, and January 39 yuan 125, with buying prices plus 125. The noon closing prices for October and November were both 39 yuan, and January 39 yuan 25. The afternoon closing prices for the near-term were 39 yuan 125, December 25, and January 375.

The domestic East Asian exchange market prices fluctuated by 75 between the front and back markets. The morning prices for October were 1 tael 2 maces 7 fen 75, November 7 fen 25, December 6 fen 75, and January 6 fen 25, with buying prices less half a fen. The noon closing prices for October were 1 tael 2 maces 7 fen 25, and January 6 fen. The afternoon closing prices for October were 1 tael 2 maces 7 fen, November 6 fen 5, December 6 fen, and January 5 fen 75, with buying prices less half a fen.

Overseas Silver Market Unmoved 161

Yesterday, according to dispatches from London, the big silver exchanges remained unchanged. Both near and far term rates were 16 and three-quarters pence, equivalent to one shilling and seven and three-quarters pence in British gold. There was a small volume of China's buy-in/buy-out foot-dragging trading, with the market generally flat. It was learned after the market closed that there was to be new financial relief for silver prices in the US. There were also dispatches from New York that US silver prices had not changed at 35.5 cents. The exchange rate between British and American currencies was also unchanged. British-English was increased by 03125, for an equivalent of 4 yuan 8 jiao 5 fen 875. Japanese-US remained at 49.5 yuan. British-English was still 2 shillings 0 jiao 4 fen 6875. The British-Shanghai shilling was still 1 shilling 7 pence and a half. Bombay spot was plus 5 ounces, for 47 rupees and 0.1 ounces. At 10:30 am yesterday, Reuters and the Tongxun Agency cables had not risen or fallen. As of the 3:35 pm cable from Tongxun, there were minor increases and decreases. The near-term rate of exchange between Japanese and US currencies did not change. The bid price increased by 0.0625, for 49 yuan 5 jiao 6 fen 25. The bid price between British and English currencies increased by 0.03125, for 2 shillings 0 jiao 4 fen 6875. The British-English offer and bid prices for far-term futures remained unadjusted. Decline of Foreign Exchange Rate Becomes More Severe 163

Sources are Numerous...Fell 3.75% Compared to the End of September

Market Overview: The market atmosphere was quite vibrant yesterday because money exchanges resumed normal operations after being closed for one day for the Mid-Autumn Festival the day before. However, the foreign exchange rate continued to fall sharply due to numerous sources. Not only did it break through the 3% threshold, but it also plummeted by more than 4% in a single day. It can be said that it was a sudden reversal of the market. As for the trivialities of silver and foreign currency collection, it goes without saying that they are being handled together for two days.

Exchange Rate Prices (Foreign Exchange): In the morning market, the market was full of suppliers due to the numerous sources the day before. As a result, the closing price fell slightly by 2%, to 73.075 cash. The afternoon market saw an even more drastic decline, with the closing price falling another 2%, to 72.85 cash. As a result, the morning market price fell as much as 3.75% compared to the end of last month. Silver Exchange (The morning market transfer account still opened at 12 cash, but the afternoon market silver exchange was only 6 cash, a difference of half. The surcharge was 2 or 3 cash, and the listed price was 5 cash.

Subsidiary Coin Market: The early market price for Jiangnan small foreign coins was 65.4 cash, and the afternoon market price was 65.45 cash. As a result, it was 1.5 cash better than the afternoon market the day before. Early market transactions amounted to 5,000 jiao, and afternoon market transactions amounted to 2,500 jiao. Guangdong small foreign coins fell with the foreign exchange rate. The early market price was 63.7 cash, and the afternoon market price was 63.5 cash. As a result, it fell by 4 cash compared to the afternoon market the day before. Early market transactions amounted to 180,000 jiao, and afternoon market transactions amounted to 100,000 jiao. Copper coins also decreased by 4,000, to 383,000 wen.

Inflow and Outflow of Silver and Foreign Currency (Silver): Yesterday's silver and money industry saw various collections of funds, which were rare in ordinary times. The fund checks and various funds were not checked in detail. It is only known that the remittance collection was more than 1 million, the closing balance was more than 5 million, and the goods funds were more than 3 million. The money exchange and silver public bills were even more impossible to verify, roughly in the range of 50 to 60 million. (Foreign Currency): Early market remittances and deputy fund checks amounted to 715,000, and afternoon market remittances amounted to 1.475 million. Banknotes were only 15,000 in the afternoon market. Off-site banknotes amounted to 123,000 in the early market and 73,000 in the afternoon market. Bank transactions amounted to 400,000 in the morning inter-market and more than 800,000 in the afternoon inter-market. The collection of foreign currency transactions between various bank foreign accounts and foreign surcharges, foreign currency borrowing, and money exchange foreign public bills were all too busy to check in detail. Small money exchange banknote remittance transactions amounted to more than 500,000, and customer sources amounted to more than 2 million.

4,000 bags of cane sugar came to Shanghai from Hong Kong,

1,900 pieces of cotton yarn were loaded and shipped to Shangjiang,

Hakodate Telegraph: The market price of kelp in each grade has continued to fall by 150 yuan to 100 yuan per 100 stones.

A Woman 173

— Chun Sen

By Ms. Ding Ling

"(A Woman)" comprises six short stories: "(A Woman and a Man)", "(After He Left)", "(Day)", "(Young Mengde's Insomnia)", "(On One Night)", and "(Wild Grass)". Naturally symbolic propositions, each piece vividly reveals the unique perspective of a woman.

(Women are mysterious)—this thought, in a certain sense, lingers in the depths of almost every man's heart. However, being a woman is probably not entirely so. If you dared to utter such a curse in front of "(A Woman)", you would surely receive a sharp retort. But let's examine "(A Woman)". The author is also "(A Woman)". Naturally, a woman writing about the actions and psychology of women will be more insightful. Although someone once wrote "(A Woman's Heart)" and earned the praise of "(This guy is really amazing)", it is still inevitably separated by a barrier. However, "(A Woman)" here is also disappointing. It elevates our women too much into a "(mysterious ivory tower)".

I often think that in those folk songs, the relationship between the sexes is expressed with genuine, unadorned, bold, and sincere emotions. They truly have the courage to sing praises, and everything is filled with youthful, bright enthusiasm. But what is expressed in the works of our so-called literary figures is always a coy attitude. They only expose the ugliness between the sexes. Popular novels about gender issues mostly construct a trap, luring men to indulge in colorful illusions, an overflowing sentimentality, enticing men to take the bait. Then, a farce that can be, yet is prevented from, being consummated plays out. It's all the same, deliberately mocking and depicting disgusting psychological reactions as if they were amusing, leaving readers with a sense of ridiculous personalities, jokes, momentary emotional impulses, stage performances, and unfinished endings.

Furthermore, are modern women all just recycled versions of those from the previous century? The women's liberation movement in China has a considerable history. But where are the representative works of that era? Especially the so-called Chinese female writers, they are merely classical poets who chant about the wind and moon, sentimentalists who moan without illness, or aesthetes who carve dragons and build tigers… The characters they portray are only morbid stereotypes. The issue of their own demands, containing bright themes, is nowhere to be seen.

After reading "(A Woman)", one truly doubts whether Chinese women are merely pitiful and irritatingly without will or ambition. Perhaps the author deliberately wrote this situation to satirize modern women in general, but the representative characters in "(A Woman)" can only make one sigh deeply, "(Chinese women are not worthy of talking about liberation)". A work that evokes a sense of disappointment is, fundamentally, also a manifestation of a morbid state.

"(A Woman and a Man)" is about a married woman (with excessive passion but unable to comprehend true love) encountering a man who drifted into prostitution (sacrificing a promising future filled with fiery hope for a woman, turning into a completely despondent and degenerate person). It is filled with the base psychological states of both sexes. I suspect you, you suspect me, half-heartedly displaying a sense of dignity. And their actions are even more secretive and incomplete. The ending is:

At the edge of Beihai, he hired a car for her. Seeing her retreating figure, he sent her another kiss in his heart. He was very happy, thinking this woman was really good. He didn't dare compare her to little Ah Jin anymore. But she was ashamed that he still didn't seem to have the courage to seize her. When she thought of his words, she felt even more ashamed. But she still couldn't decide whether she should reject this woman. He thought he should talk to Zhi Zhao about it. So he proudly jumped into a car.

As for what they ultimately gained, even he himself didn't know. He only knew that when she got into the car and gave him one last look, she coldly recalled in her heart what she had repeatedly said in the past few nights, "(He's afraid of me, he's afraid of me)". But she didn't persist in that desire. She just wanted to go home quickly. She wanted to fall into the arms of her husband, the husband she would always love. In those arms, she thought she could get everything she wanted (Page 39).

Actually, this isn't a bad subject. If the ending of the woman is taken as the main point, it could guide women with abnormal and blind love onto the right path.

"(After He Left)" is also just as boring and shallow, wasting ink by treating "(love)" as a way to have fun. One moment passionate, and the next comparing him to other men, then feeling distressed and declaring, "(I will never love him)". On one hand, she wants to accept and indulge in the insatiable pleasure of that longing; on the other hand, she feels inner sadness and conjures up many other flavorful imaginations. Even in the extreme, she remembers, "(Xiu Dong will be here soon)". But then again, "(She didn't feel bored, nor was she particularly happy. Her heart was still unusually calm, beautiful. She rested her left hand on her left cheek, and her right hand on her left arm, a faint smile on her face, she fell asleep very soundly. (Page 61)". Oh, how tortuous.

"(Day)" can only be described as an essay. In fact, how many here can be called short stories? This tells the story of a frail, sickly woman spending a tiresome and ordinary day, only hating and unconsciously enduring it, until "(Tomorrow everything will still turn around as usual)". (Page 73) In other words, she is "(willing to waste her will to live in a tiresome, ordinary, and lifeless life)".

"(Young Mengde's Insomnia)" is even more superficial. It tells the story of young Mengde fantasizing because of the arguing of the couple in the room upstairs. "(Young Mengde had a careless, very imprudent idea, actually putting himself alongside his friends and cooperating with that woman once)". (Page 82) So he couldn't sleep. He hated that short husband. Who knew that the landlord couple (were passionately making extremely unrestrained laughter)? Therefore, "(Young Mengde couldn't sleep even more)". (Page 83) So-called insomnia is nothing more than this. This article was published in "(Fiction Monthly)", but the signature at that time was not the current author. Some say it opened the precedent of "(the husband's work is the wife's, and the wife's work is the husband's)".

"(On One Night)" is the story of a young woman being flirted with by a "(man in a flesh-colored suit)". Most women nowadays endure their anger for the moment and try to avoid men because they only care about their own current situation. What is reflected here is also the same. Although she feels "(the humiliation of being played with)", she is also "(helplessly afraid)".

"(Wild Grass)" is also a fable-like story, but the description in this article is better than "(A Woman and a Man)" and "(After He Left)". The structure is also very powerful. I admit that this article is better, in terms of layout.

In short, I hope that female writers in general will never forget the demands of this great era and ignore themes of their own requirements in future creations. Because this responsibility is one that only women can bear themselves. If we continue to explore unconsciously in this area, as expressed in "(A Woman)", then I believe there will be no way out. Moreover, what is so-called contributed to our nation will only be damage. In this way, the improvement of women's status, the so-called demand for liberation, and the achievement of equality will inevitably decline.

To Wuhan 174

— Tang Bin

By Li Yizhi

The creation of Nationalist literature and art, we have already seen it in the only central publication at present (The Vanguard Weekly), which makes us feel a warm and upward-moving heart. In terms of artistic technique, it has gradually reached maturity from rich inclusion. This is a fact, because the emergence of Nationalist literature and art has both a long historical background and is oppressed by the various environments of reality. This is, of course, the severe oppression of our Chinese nation by external imperialists. Under this situation, there is no doubt that the Nationalist literature and art that scholars are actively advocating must be produced. In theory, it has undeniably laid a solid foundation, and in creation, there is also the highest expression. We must understand that as long as you are a member of the Chinese nation, you can directly experience the severe oppression of the Chinese nation from the outside. If this fact is written down with the central consciousness of nationalism, it must be a powerful and great creation that touches the hearts of readers, and will never be as shallow and empty as the so-called Proletarian literary works. This is an extremely clear fact. Mr. Yizhi's powerful work "(To Wuhan)" is worthy of our deep attention.

Judging from the historical war situation, Wuhan has become the military center of China. Even in international trade and politics, Wuhan also occupies an extremely important position. Therefore, all kinds of events within Wuhan that hinder the Chinese nation should be described with artistic techniques, and the arrogant foreigners acting arbitrarily in our China should be truthfully revealed. Everyone knows that literature and art have the greatest moving power, so literary works carved out of this kind of subject matter can inspire readers to strive forward. This kind of stimulation is of great significance, and is definitely not like the kind of literary works that are full of decadent and deteriorating central ideas, enticing readers to fall into the deep abyss of misguided depravity. Mr. Yizhi has deeply noticed this, and vividly described the evil drama of British sailors bullying Chinese people that he witnessed on the way from Jiujiang to Wuhan, containing a powerful beauty, and an upward central consciousness. The creation of Nationalist literature and art like this that promotes reader awakening is indeed a very urgent need in the current chaotic Chinese literary world. In general, this article contains such complex facts:

At that time, the Yangtze River area was at a serious time in the situation. The protagonist in the article was preparing to go from Jiujiang to Wuhan. Under the situation of "(escaping for his life)", he naturally suffered many difficult encounters. When the ship sailed to the vast river surface and saw many British warships, the sound of the giant cannons aroused a strong rebellious heart. But the protagonist, Xiao Xia, would never submit or fear in the slightest. There are also Chinese sailors who rely on the power of foreigners to oppress our people. The various cowardly psychologies of Chinese women fearing foreigners, the weaknesses of the Chinese national character shown by the vendors on the dock, the anger of the masses towards foreigners and their lackeys... are all described in order with an artistic tone, becoming a most powerful creation. Most importantly, the protagonist Xiao Xia portrayed by the author is a man with a robust beauty, and at the same time, he has a true spirit of perseverance and unyielding, and a great ambition of firm courage and striving forward. This is the characteristic that the author creates for the Chinese nation from the standpoint of Nationalist literature and art, and on the other hand, it points out the weaknesses of the old Chinese national character. This kind of subject matter is most suitable for our Chinese creators to adopt, and many powerful works should be produced.

Finally, I solemnly say that this article "(To Wuhan)" is indeed a suddenly rising creation in the current Chinese literary world. Readers who love literature and art should not neglect it in the slightest. In terms of artistic technique, it can also be regarded as a mature creation with the highest expression.

Essay Special Issue 175

— Nan Xin

Caoye Weekly, Volume 3, Number 8

Since Nationalist literature and art have been actively promoted by scholars in general, a solid foundation has long been laid in theory.

Page 20

In terms of creation, it has also gradually appeared before the eyes of readers. A large number of poems, essays, novels, dramas, and criticisms have been published in Zhoukan such as Qianfeng and Caoye. The most successful are the two categories of poetry and essays. Of course, there will be more powerful creations produced in the future, which is limitless. Now let's look at the essay special issue of Caoye Zhoukan. The content is so rich and full. In addition to the literary news, it includes six essays, with Huang Xingruo's "(Farewell)", Na E's "(Sunshine Shines on the Small Building)", and Wu Xiaotian's "(Seaside Poet)" being the best. The following are separate reviews:

New Work by Painter Pang Xunqin 176

Farewell is a description of a brave warrior, advancing with a gun in his hand on the battlefield, awakening the weak to fight for our Chinese nation and create a beautiful China. The author writes this way at the end, "(Singing songs of praise, singing about the happiness of mankind)", which is such a powerful description containing encouraging spirit. This kind of essay with an upward central consciousness is a new type of essay that must be produced in modern times. Its value is similar to that of poems with the highest artistic expression, because it is also full of extremely rich poetic emotions. "(Sunshine Shines on the Small Building)", just reading this title makes you feel the poetic flavor, arousing the inspiration to absorb literary production, and you must read this article immediately before you can satisfy your desire to appreciate literature and art. So, how vast is the power of words. The article is divided into four small sections to describe, which is actually a prose poem, with beautiful words, harmonious syllables, an upward consciousness, and a progressive portrayal. In the current Chinese literary world, it is indeed a rare work. As written in the second paragraph:

The great Chinese nation, containing the light of infinite hope before the dark clouds, expecting us who strive upwards, shaking off the courageous spirit and moving forward, like-minded people joining hands, jointly creating a beautiful garden, eliminating those blind beasts who are willing to worship others as their fathers, do not be afraid, we are fighting for the entire Chinese nation with righteousness and brightness, do not pay attention to the slanders that foreign ghosts habitually impose in the dark, we must know that we have our own will, and persevere to the end without giving in, the waves of joy fill the entire heart, and the morning sparrows are still chirping on the treetops that sway with the wind.

This is a beautiful prose poem, the extremely gorgeous words make us feel light, the natural and harmonious syllables, the upward central thought, all conform to the poetic characteristics of Nationalist literature and art. Expressing it in essays does not reduce its effectiveness in practice, and it can greatly arouse the reader's emotion. This kind of literary creation has opened up a new path in the Chinese literary world. Those who are inclined to the sentimental school and general literary lovers and creators of slogan style, I wonder what they will think after seeing this essay with a national central consciousness. In any case, I see no reason to deny its literary value. Now, I hope that Caoye will publish more of this kind of moving and beautiful essay, and I hope to publish another special issue. "(Seaside Poet)" is also a full essay, because of the limited space of this journal, readers have to appreciate it by themselves.
